**The NeedsApproval snippet no longer shows the terminal's input box and footer, just the question (BL-395).** Direct follow-on to BL-391 above, not a duplicate: BL-391 stripped *invisible* control bytes (ANSI/CSI/OSC escapes) but by its own design left visible glyphs untouched, so box-drawing rule lines, the Claude Code permission-mode/shortcut footer (`bypass permissions`, `shift+tab to cycle`, `accept edits`, `for agents`, `⏵⏵`), and a bare `❯`/`>` prompt marker still survived into the human-facing snippet — because those are printable text, not escape codes. Reported live: the human's screenshot of a `NeedsApproval` Telegram message showed a wall of `────` box-rule lines, a tofu `▯▯` glyph, and the footer furniture instead of the actual question. `extractQuestionSnippet` (`extension/src/panel/needsHumanDetection.ts`) — the single production source feeding both the Telegram send and the git-committed topic record (`backlog/topics/*.json`) — now also filters out lines that are (after BL-391's byte-strip) *unambiguously* chrome: entirely box-drawing/rule/placeholder characters, a bare prompt marker line, or the footer phrases with only connector punctuation left over once those phrases are removed. The neighbour guard from BL-391 carries over: a line is dropped only when it is chrome and nothing else, so a real question line — even one containing a dash or the word "for" — is never touched, and ordinary prose passes through byte-identical. No human-visible command or setting changed.

**A topic's icon now tracks its ticket's state instead of rotting (BL-342).** Telegram never hides a closed topic — it stays in the list forever, so with the list growing without bound the icon is the only per-topic signal that separates history from live work at a glance. The human had hand-applied a convention across 26 ticket topics himself (✅ done, 🦠 defect in flight, 💡 feature in flight, 🔍 paused/held); nothing in the swarm knew icons existed, so the convention would have started lying the moment the first ticket shipped after it was set. `editForumTopic` and `getForumTopicIconStickers` (`telegramClient.ts`) are new wrappers — only `createForumTopic`/`closeForumTopic` existed before this, and an icon id is only ever valid if resolved against the real, live-fetched sticker set (112 today), never hardcoded; `createForumTopic` also gained an optional initial-icon parameter, and a 429's own `retry_after` now surfaces on the shared API result instead of being swallowed into an opaque failure. `topicIcon.ts` resolves a ticket's folder (active/paused/done) plus its `type` into one of the four states above — done/paused are authoritative over `type` (a paused bug still shows the magnifier, a shipped bug still shows the check). A durable `swarmIconId` marker on each ticket's `blTopicStore.ts` record is the "did the swarm set this icon" flag: absent means never touch it, whether a human customised it or its origin is simply unknown, since there is no live read API to tell the two apart — `topicIconSync.ts`'s `syncTopicIcon` lets a brand-new topic take its initial icon freely but only updates an existing one when the marker shows the swarm already owns it. Icon sync is wired into `conciergeTick.ts` on its own independent folder-membership diff, deliberately NOT riding `deriveSwarmEvents`' `TaskStarted`/`TaskCompleted` dedup — a first draft that piggybacked directly on those events silently failed to restore a ticket's icon after a pause-then-re-promote, since that dedup key never re-fires once emitted; caught by a re-promotion test. `backfill-topic-icons.ts` is a one-time CLI that seeds the marker across every existing ticket topic, honouring a 429's `retry_after` exactly and retrying the same topic unboundedly — the human's own hand pass had hit the rate limit after 19 of 26 calls and silently dropped the rest.

**The feature-in-flight topic icon is now a musical note, not a light bulb (BL-417).** Part of a human design session remapping ticket-topic icons toward an orchestra theme (`docs/branding/icon-system.md` §5a); the rest of that theme rides other, separate tickets. Telegram's free `getForumTopicIconStickers` set (112 stickers, live-checked 2026-07-15) has no instrument/notation glyphs, so only one of BL-342's four states had a musical stand-in: `topicIcon.ts`'s `ICON_EMOJI.feature` changes from 💡 to 🎵 ("a passage being played"); done ✅, defect 🦠, and paused 🔍 are unchanged, since nothing in the live set beats them. `resolveIconState` itself is untouched — this is a one-value change to the existing lookup table, reusing BL-342's machinery rather than adding new machinery, and keeps the same resolve-or-skip-if-absent posture against the live sticker set (never a hardcoded custom-emoji id) so a future set change degrades gracefully instead of crashing a tick. A backfill run (`backfill-topic-icons.ts`, unchanged) reglyphs existing feature topics to 🎵.

**The standing (non-ticket) Telegram topics now carry their own orchestra icons instead of staying icon-blank forever (BL-418).** The harder half of the same human design session as BL-417 above: BL-342's icon sync fires only on ticket-level folder/type transitions, so the support/intake topic(s) and the standing Operator topic had no icon logic touching them at all. `topicIcon.ts` gains a second, separate lookup — `STANDING_TOPIC_ICON` (`'support/intake': 🎟`, `operator: 🏛`, both human-decided 2026-07-15, both confirmed present in the live 112-sticker set) — kept apart from `ICON_EMOJI` since neither standing key is a ticket folder/type. `conciergeTick.ts`'s new `syncStandingTopicIcons` sets a standing topic's icon only the first time that topic's id is ever seen (a durable `standingIconSeenIds` set on `TickState`, the standing-topic sibling of the ticket-icon sync's own before/after diff) — a standing topic is never "created" by a tick the way a ticket topic is, so this durable seen-set is what tells a genuinely new appearance apart from a pre-existing topic that may already carry a human-customised icon; once seen, a standing topic is never re-set on a later tick, preserving BL-342's "never overwrite an icon the swarm didn't set" rule for topics the swarm now touches at all. `backfill-standing-topic-icons.ts` is a new one-time CLI, mirroring `backfill-topic-icons.ts` (BL-342), that seeds every currently-open standing topic's icon and seeds `standingIconSeenIds` in the same pass, so the live tick never re-treats an already-backfilled topic as newly entered. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** added coverage for a transient `setTopicIcon` failure on a standing topic's first tick — it still marks the topic seen rather than retrying on the live path, matching this module's existing best-effort posture for per-ticket icon sync and epic-progress posts; recovery for that case is a re-run of the backfill script. No new human-facing command; a support/intake or Operator topic without a human-set icon now shows 🎟/🏛 instead of staying blank.

**A paused ticket's Telegram topic now shows a distinct icon when it's the human's own approval blocking it (BL-424).** Before this, `resolveIconState` (`topicIcon.ts`) mapped every paused ticket to the same plain 🔍, whether it was held on a dependency, an overlap serialisation, a deliberate park, or — the one case actionable by the human right now — his own pending sign-off; from the topic list there was no way to tell them apart at a glance. `TopicIconState` gains a fifth, paused-scoped member, `'awaiting-approval'` (👀); `resolveIconState` takes an optional `humanApproval` argument and returns it only when `folder === 'paused' && humanApproval === 'pending'` — every other paused ticket (approved, or the field absent) still gets the plain 🔍, and an active or done ticket is untouched even if its approval field were somehow pending, since the folder gates the state, not the field alone. `syncTopicIcon` (`topicIconSync.ts`) gains an optional `fallbackEmoji`: if 👀 is ever absent from the live sticker set, it resolves the ordinary paused icon instead of skipping the topic outright, so the worst case is indistinguishable from a normal paused ticket rather than a missing icon. `conciergeTick.ts`'s `syncIconForBacklogId` now also reads each ticket's `human_approval` off the same folder snapshot `typeForBacklogId` already reads (never a second derivation) and passes it through; `backfill-topic-icons.ts` does the same for its one-time seed pass. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** Gherkin acceptance mutation ran clean (20/20 killed). No new human-facing command; a paused ticket awaiting the human's own approval now shows 👀 instead of 🔍, and reverts to 🔍 once approved or promoted.

**The front desk now filters inbound Telegram updates on chat, not just sender (BL-379).** `decideUpdateAction` never consulted `update.message.chat` — Telegram's `getUpdates` is scoped to the *bot*, not to any one chat, so a second project's group added to the same bot could silently cross-wire its messages into this project's own support threads via BL-294's auto-adopt (the same message-loss/mis-routing class as BL-369/370/371, just via a different channel). `isFromMyChat` (`telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts`) is a new, first-checked guard in `decideUpdateAction`: a message from a foreign chat now drops with reason `not-my-chat`, checked *before* the existing principal check, since a stranger in a foreign chat should read as "wrong chat," never "wrong sender" — proven with a dedicated priority-order test, since both conditions can hold at once in the wild. The bot's configured chat id lives on `PollAdapters` as a plain config field (`chatId`) rather than a new threaded parameter, keeping the change confined to adapter fixtures instead of every call site along `processUpdate`/`pollAndForward`/`runPollCycle`. No new human-facing command or setting; this closes a cross-project message-leak class in the same front-desk isolation family as BL-334/BL-369.

**A topic record's git commit now survives a transient index-lock race instead of silently never happening (BL-407).** Observed live: 26 distinct done tickets (BL-305..328, BL-333, BL-334) sat past their retention window with `topicDeletion.ts` correctly refusing to delete their Telegram topics, because none of them had a verified-committed completion record — `topicDeletion.ts`'s refusal guard itself was never wrong. Root cause, confirmed against the live front-desk-supervisor log's own "FAILED to commit topic record" lines: `commitScopedFile` (`gitCommitScopedFile.ts`) made exactly one `git add`+`commit` attempt, and the front-desk bot process shares one physical worktree with the coordinator/specifier, so a momentary collision on `.git/index.lock` turned into a *permanent* durability gap for that record — the content on disk was byte-correct the whole time, just never committed. `commitScopedFile` now retries a bounded number of times with backoff before giving up (the same bounded-retry posture the engineering article already requires of any retry loop), with the attempt function and sleep both injected so the test drives the retry deterministically rather than waiting on a real lock race. `repair-bl-topic-records.ts` now also backfills this durability-only gap — committing an already-correct record it previously skipped as "opener-already-present" — covering the one real offender (BL-334) that needed no content repair, just a commit. `topicDeletion.ts` itself is unchanged. Reconciling the real 26 affected topics is a separate operational step (running `repair-bl-topic-records.js` against the live master checkout, not from an isolated worktree) — no human-visible command or setting changed by this ticket itself.

**A proactive Telegram alert now fires before the swarm's disk fills, instead of the swarm crashing into ENOSPC (BL-412).** Live incident, overnight 2026-07-14/15: a full disk took the whole swarm down — agents crash mid-write, handoff parcels and topic records get truncated, and the logs that would explain it can't be written either. `disk_space_lib.bb` is a new pure decision function (per-filesystem `df` reading + thresholds + prior last-announced level → transitions/messages/next-state) wired into `operator_runtime.bb`'s existing always-alive tick as `disk-space-sweep!` — no new daemon. It watches two filesystems independently, since a Windows-host VHDX-on-C: setup means one can be nearly full while the other reads healthy: the WSL root (percent-used: WARN ≥ 90%, CRITICAL ≥ 95%) and `/mnt/c`, the Windows volume actually backing the dynamically-growing VHDX (absolute free space: WARN < 40 GB, CRITICAL < 15 GB). Change-gated on the BL-394 lesson — an alert fires only on a level transition (healthy→warn, warn→critical, and recovery back down) per filesystem, with the last-announced level persisted so an unchanged reading is never re-announced tick after tick. Delivery reuses the existing operator notify path (`operator_notify.bb`'s reply-outbox, the reserved `OPERATOR` thread) — the same standing-Operator-topic route the human-approved `disk_alert.sh` cron stopgap already used. **Go-live step, not yet done:** once this ships, a human/QA must delete `.swarmforge/operator/disk_alert.sh` and its crontab line (`crontab -l | grep -v disk_alert | crontab -`) — the interim stopgap stays running until that manual removal happens.

**A leaked `/tmp`-rooted daemon can no longer send a real briefing email (BL-406).** Live incident, morning of 2026-07-15: the human received 3-4 duplicate morning briefings, inconsistently in French or English and with or without diagrams. Root cause: not one sender misfiring, but **seven** `handoffd.bb` processes alive at send time — the legitimate project-rooted daemon plus six leaked from stale `/tmp` acceptance-test sandboxes (alive 9-11 hours, unsupervised), each independently sweeping and sending its own real briefing email; four differently-timed, differently-resolved sends explains both the duplication and the inconsistency in one root cause, as the ticket's investigation theorized. The existing `test-fixture-root?` guard (BL-326) only suppressed the *send* for a `/tmp`-rooted project, per-email, and did nothing for a daemon-level side effect that never reaches it (a push sweep, an Operator/Telegram relay, a GitHub issue close). `daemon_alarm_lib.bb` adds a pure `refuse-tmp-daemon-start?` predicate; `handoffd.bb` now checks it before claiming a pid file, loading roles, or starting a single sweep, so a leaked or mistaken invocation against a `/tmp`-rooted root exits immediately instead of running unsupervised for hours. Opt-in for the wiring tests that intentionally run a real daemon under a throwaway root: set `SWARMFORGE_ALLOW_TMP_DAEMON=1` (any non-blank value opts in, including `"0"` — only a blank/whitespace-only value still refuses). No human-visible command or setting changed; this is a defense-in-depth daemon-startup guard, plus a same-pass hardening fix for a wiring test the new guard broke and two locked-in flag-value edge cases.

**A ticket's Telegram topic title now carries a coarse, change-gated "last updated" age suffix (BL-414).** The icon already carries ticket STATE (BL-342) and a colour gradient isn't achievable in Telegram, so at the human's own request the topic TITLE instead gets a glanceable staleness cue: `"BL-999 do a thing · 3h ago"`, `"· 2d ago"`, `"· 3d+ ago"`, or no suffix at all inside the first hour. `topicTitleAge.ts` is the pure decision half — `stalenessBucket`/`decideTitleAge` bucket elapsed time since the ticket's last activity (`blTopicStore`'s own last-activity timestamp, not a new store) into `fresh` (<1h, no suffix) / `hours` (1-24h, "Nh ago") / `day` (1-3d, "Nd ago") / `stale` (>3d, "3d+ ago"), and — mirroring BL-342's icon change-gate — only return a new title when the bucket actually changed from the caller's last-announced bucket, so a topic sitting mid-bucket is never re-edited tick after tick. `composeTitleWithAge` always strips any existing "· ... ago" tail before re-appending (`AGE_SUFFIX_PATTERN`) so the suffix can never accumulate and the underlying ticket title is always preserved intact; new activity resets a topic to the `fresh` bucket on its next tick, which visibly *removes* a previously-shown stale suffix rather than replacing it. `topicTitleSync.ts` is the adapter-injected I/O half, wired into `conciergeTick.ts`'s existing per-tick loop (`syncAllTitleAgeBuckets`, extracted to its own helper alongside `syncStandingTopicIcons`/`syncIconForBacklogId` to keep `runConciergeTick`'s own CRAP at its BL-424 baseline) the same way BL-342's icon sync already rides that loop, editing only concierge-owned topics and never crashing the tick over a cosmetic rename. **Hardener bounce, same ticket:** the first cut fired one unthrottled `editForumTopic` per ticket on every tick, and on the very first tick (or after any state loss) every one of the repo's 113 tracked topics transitions from an unset bucket to a real one at once — the exact "19 of 26 succeeded, rest silently dropped" Telegram rate-limit storm `backfill-topic-icons.ts` had already hit once, reproduced at roughly 4x the scale. Fixed by generalizing that backfill's own 429/`retry_after`-honoring retry loop into a shared `editForumTopicWithRateLimitRetry` (`telegramClient.ts`), which the icon backfill now delegates to instead of duplicating, and which the live title-age sync adapter uses too — proven with a wiring test that seeds 30 tickets (over the historical 26-topic trip threshold) with unset buckets in one tick and simulates a mid-batch 429. No new human-facing command or setting; a concierge-managed ticket topic's title now grows a staleness suffix as it goes untouched, and loses it again the moment someone posts.

**The human now has an offline answer channel: `ANSWER-*.md` files, committed and pushed, drained through a stale-premise gate (BL-440).** Closes an asymmetry in the human-in-the-loop: the swarm's asks are already durable offline (BL-329's git-committed BL topics), but the human's only way to answer one away from Telegram was hand-editing ticket YAML. `drain-answer-files.ts` (`node drain-answer-files.js <repo-root>`) drains any `ANSWER-*.md` file committed at the backlog root — symmetric with the existing `INTAKE-*.md` convention — with a deliberately forgiving schema: no required header syntax, just a `BL-###` ticket id mentioned anywhere in the file, with the file's whole trimmed content carried through as the human's own words. **The gate is mandatory, no bypass:** an answer is acted on only when the ticket it references is still open (not in `backlog/done/`, not itself `status: done`) — a closed reference never executes; instead it is reported "arrived late, not executed" so a late answer can never blind-execute against a premise that already moved on, the same failure class that once let an escalation resurrect an already-retracted question. An unresolvable reference (no parseable `BL-###` anywhere) is reported "unresolved" and, having no ticket to attach a record to, is deliberately left in place rather than archived — BL-311's own "an un-drained file signals itself by still being there" convention. Both outcomes append to the referenced ticket's own git-committed BL-topic record (`blTopicStore.ts`, BL-329), which projects into the live Telegram topic when connected and stands as the committed note otherwise — no new report surface. A successfully-acted-on answer's file is moved to `backlog/answers-archive/`, archived rather than deleted, mirroring BL-311's intake hygiene. **Architect bounce, same ticket:** the first cut shipped `drainAnswerFiles` with no production caller — only its own CLI and its tests ever invoked it, so a committed `ANSWER-*.md` was never actually drained unless a human ran the CLI by hand. Fixed by wiring an `answer-file-drain-sweep!` into `handoffd.bb`'s existing poll loop, on the same cadence as its other `*-sweep!`s (fleet-status, push, resource-sample), so draining now happens automatically on reconnect/pull rather than requiring a manual run. Explicitly out of scope for this slice: a PWA compose surface and email inbound (both deferred to a possible later slice). **QA bounce: the stale-premise gate now checks the SPECIFIC pending question, not just the ticket.** The original gate only checked ticket-level status/folder, so a ticket that stayed `active`/`todo` throughout while the swarm retracted or superseded its one pending question was still reported live — a stale answer to that retracted question would have been silently accepted as an ordinary inbound message. `blTopicStore.ts` gains a structured per-question signal: an outbound message can carry `retractsPendingQuestion: true`, and `hasRetractedPendingQuestion(record)` is true only when the LATEST message (by seq) is such a retraction — an earlier retraction the swarm has since moved past (e.g. asked again) does not count. `checkPremiseLive` checks this signal after its existing folder/status guards. **The retraction flag now has a real writer, not just test fixtures.** A successful gate answer (`operator_runtime.bb`'s `bl-topic-approval-sweep!` → `operator-decide.js <backlogId> approve`, the consumer of a human reply typed into a ticket's own topic) is the real decision point where that ticket's pending question stops being live — this now threads `retractsPendingQuestion` from that approval path through the reply-outbox/SSE relay to the same `appendMessage` call that already records the confirmation reply, so every real answer path sets the flag, not only hand-built tests. **A human-facing runbook (BL-441) walks through using this channel:** `docs/how-to/BL-441-answering-offline-runbook.md` — reading a pending question from the committed BL topics (`backlog/topics/*.json`), composing and pushing an `ANSWER-*.md`, and the stale-premise caveat. The PWA does **not** currently surface pending-question state (it fetches only `backlog.json`/`docs-tree.json`/`recert-batch.json`, none of which carry that signal — its one human-facing flag, `needsApproval`, is the unrelated swarm-proposal-review mechanism), so the runbook relies on the BL topic files, not the PWA, for offline reading.

**A natural-language contract approval no longer gets misread as an objection and spliced into the contract as a fabricated clause (BL-442).** Live incident, first real end-to-end FES onboarding run 2026-07-15: the human replied "All agreed" in the negotiation topic (BL-381), and because `AGREEMENT_PATTERN`'s anchored `^\s*(agree|agreed|approve|approved|lgtm|yes)[.!]?\s*$` only matched a single bare word, "All agreed" fell through to the objection path — running an unrequested revision round whose `objectToContract` then blind-appended the reply text itself as a new contract boundary line (`"- Per operator objection: All agreed"`), so the contract the human had just approved carried a clause fabricated from the approval that approved it. Two independent fixes, both required: (a) `AGREEMENT_PATTERN` (`negotiationTelegramRouting.ts`) is broadened to also recognize common short natural-language approvals ("all agreed", "ok", "okay") while keeping the pre-existing substring guard intact — an objection that merely *contains* an approval word ("I don't agree that...") is still classified as an objection, never approval; a reply matching neither the approval nor a recognizable-objection shape now lands in a new ambiguous bucket that asks the human to disambiguate in the topic instead of silently running a revision. (b) `reviseContractFromObjection`'s blind-append fallback is removed outright — a revision that cannot derive a concrete contract change from the reply text now leaves the contract byte-unchanged and posts back "couldn't derive a change from this — rephrase?" rather than writing the raw reply as a line; a revision that *can* derive a real change still collapses the embedded reply text to a single line before splicing it in (the BL-409 sibling rule: external text entering a structured file must never carry a raw newline across a line boundary). No new human-facing command; a natural-language "yes" now just ends the negotiation, and no reply — approval or objection — can ever appear verbatim as a contract clause.

**The onboarding contract commit step now actually lands in an arbitrary foreign target, instead of requiring manual git surgery (BL-443).** First real end-to-end FES onboarding run, 2026-07-15: every one of `propose-onboarding-contract`'s three commit-path assumptions broke against a real foreign checkout, and each was worked around by hand at the time. All three fixes live in the one shared seam every bootstrap artifact already commits through (`writeFilesAndCommit`/`writeAndCommitBootstrapPlan`, `extension/src/config/targetBootstrap.ts`). (1) A target whose `.gitignore`/`.git/info/exclude` ignores `.swarmforge/` (FES carried a stale June-era exclude) used to hard-fail `git add` outright — the commit now force-adds exactly the contract paths it just wrote (`git add -f -- .swarmforge/contract.yaml CONTRACT.md`), never a broad `-f`, so an inherited ignore rule can no longer silently re-hold the onboarding gate on every fresh clone. (2) A target with no `user.name`/`user.email` configured anywhere (common on a brand-new or foreign checkout) used to die "Author identity unknown" — the commit now falls back to an explicit identity (`SwarmForge <noreply@swarmforge>`) via `git -c user.name=... -c user.email=...` only when none is configured, and logs that the fallback was used. (3) The existence-only idempotency check used to treat "the file is on disk" as "done," so once defect (1) or (2) aborted a commit, every subsequent re-run reported `committed:false` forever — no number of re-runs ever recovered. The check is now existence-AND-committed (queries `git ls-files`/status for exactly the written paths), so a written-but-uncommitted artifact from a prior partial failure now actually gets committed on the next run, while BL-382's `git diff --cached --quiet` no-op guard still keeps a genuinely-already-committed re-run a clean no-op with no empty commit. No new human-facing command; onboarding a foreign target's contract no longer needs hand git surgery.

**Channel provisioning now follows a group-to-supergroup migration instead of latching the dead pre-migration chat id forever (BL-444).** First real run of `provision-onboarding-telegram-channel` against a genuinely foreign target (free-email-scanner via `@fes_swarm_bot`), 2026-07-15: `decideChannelDetection` (`telegramChannelProvisioning.ts`) picked the FIRST chat id any `getUpdates` batch carried — but the CLI's own documented setup instructions ("create a group ... then enable Topics") are exactly what causes Telegram to silently upgrade a basic group to a supergroup with a brand-new id, emitting `migrate_to_chat_id` updates. The update queue still starts with the dead pre-migration group's own updates, so detection latched that dead id and provisioning failed identically on every re-run — first "the chat is not a forum," then "group chat was upgraded to a supergroup chat" — because the CLI's `getUpdates` offset was hardcoded to `0` on every call, so a re-run always re-saw the same poisoned queue from the start. This is the documented happy path, not an edge case: only a group created as a forum from the outset avoids the migration. Detection now scans every update and follows the newest `migrate_to_chat_id`/`migrate_from_chat_id` signal seen, rather than trusting the first chat id encountered; a `createForumTopic` "upgraded to a supergroup" error now surfaces its own `parameters.migrate_to_chat_id` and provisioning treats it as a redirect to retry against, not a terminal failure; and the CLI persists its `getUpdates` offset, confirming it past every consumed update once provisioning fully succeeds, so a later re-run never re-observes the stale pre-migration queue that poisoned it before. No new human-facing command or setup step — the documented "create a group, then enable Topics" flow is unchanged; it now actually converges.

**Every swarm role now has its own standing Telegram steering topic, and any authorised message posted in it interrupts that role's live pane — no `!` marker required yet (BL-425 slice 1).** Generalizes the single standing Operator topic (BL-346) from one shared channel into ONE topic per role — all 8 (the 7 pipeline roles plus the coordinator, which sits outside `PIPELINE_CHAIN`'s forward chain but still gets its own topic) — a new class of topic alongside the existing per-ticket BL topics and the Operator topic, not a repurposing of either. `ensureRoleTopics` (`telegram-front-desk-bot.ts`) creates each role's forum topic (named for the role) on first sight and records it in a NEW machine-local map, `.swarmforge/operator/role-topic-map.json` (`roleTopicMapStore.ts`, gitignored host-persisted state, keyed by role name directly — no reserved-subject indirection the way the single shared Operator topic needs one). Called once before the poll loop starts, same ordering rationale as `ensureOperatorTopic`: no inbound message can reach an unbound role topic and be misrouted while it is still unbound; one role's failed create is logged and skipped, never blocking the rest. This slice ships REDIRECT mode only — an explicit, DISRUPTIVE steering message. `decideSteeringAction` (`telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts`) is the pure inbound decision: a message whose topic is not one of the eight role topics is `ignore` (checked first, so the existing BL-ticket/Operator/SUP routing is reached completely untouched — those topics keep their existing behavior); only inside a role topic does the principal guard (BL-239/240's `isFromMyChat`/`isFromPrincipal`, reused verbatim) apply, distinguishing an unauthorised sender (`refuse`, no nudge) from the authorised human (`redirect`). `redirectToRole` (`telegram-front-desk-bot.ts`) executes an authorised redirect as a VERIFIED, INTERRUPTING nudge into role R's live tmux pane via `swarm/verifiedInject.ts`'s `sendInstructionVerified` (never a bare unverified `Enter`, BL-152) on the swarm's own tmux socket (`.swarmforge/tmux-socket`) — the same seam the daily-briefing/idle-clear nudges already inject through, never the restricted front-desk operator's own socket (BL-334). Routing is exact: role R's topic reaches only role R's pane, resolved fresh per redirect via `resolveRolePaneTarget`, never another role's. A redirect against a not-yet-running swarm (no live pane resolved) degrades to a logged no-op rather than throwing. **Not yet built (parked in the companion `.feature.draft` until BL-233 promotes it):** the non-disruptive QUESTION mode — a plain (unmarked) message queued to the agent as a mailbox note it answers back into the topic without pulling it off its task, plus the `!`-prefix mode selector that will make an unmarked message default to QUESTION instead of always resolving to REDIRECT as it does in this slice. No new human-facing command; eight new standing topics appear per swarm (specifier, coder, cleaner, architect, hardender, documenter, QA, coordinator), and any authorised message posted in one interrupts that role's pane on its phone-visible topic — marked or not, since the `!`-prefix mode selector does not exist yet in this slice.

**Epic Telegram topics now carry distinct musical-form icons instead of their old hand-set trophy/lightning/folder icons (BL-449).** Codifies a human directive: an epic is a large-scale musical FORM, so its icon comes from that vocabulary — realised on two distinct surfaces, since Telegram can't carry the same art the PWA/fleet-console/bot-avatar surfaces do (`docs/branding/icon-system.md` §4d's owned orchestra FORM marks are arbitrary SVGs, and Telegram topic icons may only be stock stickers from the free `getForumTopicIconStickers` set, which has no notation/instrument glyphs at all — see the new rule in `swarmforge/constitution/articles/local-engineering.prompt`). A new, deliberately separate module (`epicIcon.ts`) holds an ordered musical-form performance-emoji pool (headed by 🎙 BENCHMARKING / 🎭 DYNAMIC_ROUTING / 🎬 ONBOARDING) and `resolveEpicIcon`, disjoint from both the ticket-state `ICON_EMOJI` (BL-342/417) and the standing-topic `STANDING_TOPIC_ICON` (BL-418) pools — epics are explicitly kept out of BL-342's ticket-state icon sync, since an epic topic is neither a ticket folder nor a standing topic. A newly-created epic topic is auto-assigned the next distinct pool icon at creation time (`conciergeTick.ts`'s epic-topic create path); pool exhaustion degrades to a logged, graceful reuse rather than a crash. The same resolve-or-skip posture as every other icon path applies: an emoji absent from the live sticker set is skipped, never sent as an unvalidated custom emoji id. Ownership is unchanged from BL-342's rule — the live tick only sets/updates an epic icon the swarm already owns, or a brand-new epic topic's initial icon; a human-recustomised epic icon is left alone. `backfill-epic-topic-icons.ts` is a new one-time CLI, modelled on the existing standing/ticket backfills, that is the one authorised override: it sets all three seeded epics' icons even though their current hand-assigned icons are not swarm-owned, and seeds the live tick's seen-set so it never re-treats a backfilled epic as newly-entered. No new human-facing command; the three existing epic topics (Swarm Role Benchmarking, Dynamic Routing, Onboarding a New Target Repo) show 🎙/🎭/🎬 once the backfill runs, and any future epic topic gets the next distinct performance sticker automatically.

**A live pipeline-board grid now shows every active ticket's current stage in its own standing Telegram topic (BL-452).** An Operator directive relayed 2026-07-16, jumping the paused queue: a lowkey glanceable kanban — active BL tickets on the Y axis, pipeline roles on the X axis, a single `X` mark at each ticket's current stage — real-time (reflects a stage change within a concierge tick), read-only, and living inside the front-desk bot rather than a separate service. The Operator asked for the bridge's `/pipeline` state specifically, not the handoff hop-log, but `readPipelineStages` (`swarmState.ts`) reported only each role's busy/idle status with no per-ticket data; the specifier surfaced this as the ticket's one real design fork and the human resolved it via `AskUserQuestion` (re-affirmed once more, 2026-07-16, against a follow-up "could the coordinator push instead?" — rejected, since the coordinator sits outside the forward chain and cannot author every stage transition, and the tick already polls, so pushing would just duplicate the handoff mailbox as a second source of truth): **enrich** `PipelineStage` with each role's currently-`in_process`-held ticket id(s), a cheap one-directory read, never a git-history walk. `readInProcessTicketIds` reuses the existing batch-aware handoff-header reader (`readHandoffHeaderRecordsWithBatches`/`extractTicketId`) already relied on by `ticketHoldingWindows.ts`, deliberately distinct from that module's own "current holder," which derives from completed+in_process holding *windows* — the hop-log-shaped mechanism the Operator explicitly rejected as this feature's data source. `pipelineBoard.ts` is the pure render half: `computePipelineBoardRows` places every role-held ticket first (in `PIPELINE.md`'s own role order) then every paused ticket, in its `parked` or (BL-424's own paused-scoped signal) `awaiting-approval` status column, so every active ticket lands in exactly one row with no empty rows; `renderPipelineBoard` renders a monospace grid (two-letter column glyphs — `SP CO CL AR HD DC QA CD PK AA` — sized for a phone screen) wrapped in a Telegram HTML `<pre>` block. `pipelineBoardSync.ts` is the adapter-injected I/O half: edge-triggered on the rendered *text* changing (never on any one ticket's transition), it posts once to a standing "Pipeline Board" topic (created once, its id persisted in `TickState.pipelineBoard`, the same durable-marker posture `standingIconSeenIds`/`titleAgeBuckets` already use) and edits that same message in place on every subsequent change — never re-posted, never re-edited when nothing changed, so it cannot trigger the first-tick rate-limit storm `backfill-topic-icons.ts` (BL-342) once hit, since this is always a single message, not a per-topic fan-out. `telegramClient.ts` gained `editMessageText` (message-id-addressed, distinct from `editForumTopic`'s topic-id-addressed rename/re-icon) and an optional `parse_mode` on `sendMessage`, both additive and behavior-preserving for every existing caller. Wired into `conciergeTick.ts` as a fully optional adapter pair (`readRoleHeldTickets`/`boardAdapters`), so every existing fixture across the codebase's acceptance step handlers keeps working unchanged. **Cleaner pass, same ticket:** extracted `resolveBoardTopicId`/`postOrEditBoard` out of `syncPipelineBoard` and a `syncBoardIfWired` helper out of `runConciergeTick` to bring both back under the CRAP<=6 gate, behavior-preserving. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** covered `readInProcessTicketIds` against an in_process handoff with no `task` field at all and one whose `task` field doesn't parse to a ticket id — both must be omitted, not thrown; a soft Gherkin id-mutation pass over the ticket's own Scenario Outline intentionally survives 4 mutants of the `<id>` example value, since `renderPipelineBoard` treats a ticket id as an opaque passthrough string (never validated against a closed set the way `<state>`/`<column>` are), a documented equivalent-mutant case, not a coverage gap. No new human-facing command; a "Pipeline Board" Telegram topic now appears alongside the standing Operator/support topics, showing at a glance which stage holds each active ticket.

**Refinement, same feature (BL-455):** the board now groups its stage-grid rows by epic (deterministic sort), and a ticket that is `parked`/`awaiting-approval` no longer occupies a grid column at all — it moves into a separate list below the grid instead, so those two statuses are never grid columns. Every row (grid or below-grid) also carries a short slug derived from the ticket's own title, so a glance at the board no longer requires opening the ticket to know roughly what it is. `PipelineBoardRow` grew `epic`/`slug` fields; `conciergeTick.ts`'s `syncBoardIfWired` joins each role-held/paused ticket id to its backlog item's epic and title from the already-loaded folders snapshot — no new git-history walk.

**Refinement, same feature (BL-462):** three further human-requested tweaks to the live board, from the front desk via the Operator — a wider slug, an "updated at" footer, and repost-at-bottom so the board is always the topic's latest message. `PIPELINE_BOARD_SLUG_MAX_LENGTH` widened from 24 to 40; `renderPipelineBoard(data, lastChangeMs)` now appends an `updated at MMM DD HH:MM` footer (UTC, via the pure `formatUpdatedAtLabel`) below the grid, fed the last CONTENT-change instant, never the current clock. The change-gate moved from "did the rendered text change" to a two-part signature: `renderPipelineBoardBody` (the grid + parked list, deliberately EXCLUDING the footer) is the persisted `contentSignature` compared tick over tick, so a tick where nothing but the wall clock advanced changes neither the footer nor the message. `pipelineBoardSync.ts` no longer delegates to `syncEditInPlaceMessage`: on an unchanged signature it does nothing at all; on a changed signature it records the injected instant as the new last-change time, renders body+footer, deletes the previous board message (if any, via `telegramClient.ts`'s new `deleteMessage`) and posts a fresh one — always the newest message in the topic. `TickState.pipelineBoard` grew `contentSignature`/`lastChangeMs` alongside its existing `topicId`/`messageId`. The Approvals Roster (`approvalsRosterSync.ts`) is unchanged and still edits in place — only the board moved to repost-at-bottom; `editInPlaceMessageSync.ts` itself was not touched. No new human-facing command; the same "Pipeline Board" Telegram topic now shows a wider per-ticket slug, an updated-at footer, and reposts to the bottom of the topic only when a ticket's stage actually changes.

**Bug fix, same feature (BL-464): the board's active rows now come from an authoritative coordinator-fed store, not an in_process scrape — closing both a missing-ticket defect and the double-row defect at the source.** The human, via the Operator front desk, reported the live board "defeats the purpose": tickets a role was ACTIVELY WORKING (BL-434, BL-450) never appeared, and BL-460 rendered on two rows at once during a stage transition. Root cause: BL-452's `readInProcessTicketIds` extracted a ticket id only from a `git_handoff`'s `task:` header, so a ticket kicked off by the coordinator's promote-via-note convention (which carries no `task:` header) was invisible until it became a downstream `git_handoff`; and pushing one row per `(role, id)` observation with no cross-role dedupe let the same ticket render twice while momentarily held at two roles. The human chose the coordinator-fed fix (`AskUserQuestion` Q2) over a smaller note-aware scraper, since the coordinator already tracks parcel location end to end. New Babashka module `pipeline_stage_lib.bb` (pure) reconciles each active role's in_process handoff — a `git_handoff`'s `task` header OR a `note`'s `message` header, closing the note-kickoff blind spot — down to exactly one role per ticket, favoring the most-downstream role on a transient two-role overlap; `pipeline_stage_cli.bb report|sync` is its one shell-callable entry point, writing the reconciled `{ticket-id: role}` map atomically to `.swarmforge/board/ticket-stage-map.json`. `swarmforge/roles/coordinator.prompt` now instructs the coordinator to run `sync` after every promotion/routing/bookkeeping/queue-sweep action — the coordinator is the real production writer this store needs, per the engineering article's named-writer/reader rule. `extension/src/swarm/swarmState.ts`'s new `readTicketStageMap`/`invertTicketStageToRoleHeldTickets` read that store and replace `telegram-front-desk-bot.ts`'s prior `readPipelineStages`-derived scrape as the board's `readRoleHeldTickets` adapter (`readPipelineStages` itself is unchanged — the VS Code panel's own `currentStageLabel`/holder logic still uses it). `computePipelineBoard` also now collapses a duplicate ticket id across roles to one row (most-downstream wins) as a belt-and-braces renderer guarantee, structurally redundant with but independent of the store's own one-role-per-ticket shape. No new human-facing command; the same "Pipeline Board" Telegram topic now shows every actively-worked ticket (including a freshly note-promoted one) at its true current stage, always on exactly one row.

**Shell and Babashka test harnesses now clean up their own temp dirs (BL-459, the BL-420 prevention gap).** BL-420 made the extension's Vitest suite self-clean its own `mkdtemp` dirs, but the shell (`swarmforge/scripts/test/*.sh`) and Babashka (`*_test_runner.bb`) test harnesses had no cleanup trap at all, feeding a `/tmp` accumulation of stale `sfvc-*`/`aps-*` directories an Operator directive flagged (~377k dirs, ~5.3M inodes). This is internal test-infrastructure hygiene with no human-facing command or setting. A shared `swarmforge/scripts/test/lib/tmp_cleanup.sh` registers one `EXIT` trap per script; calling `register_tmp_dir "$var"` right after each `mktemp -d` assignment adds it to that trap's cleanup list, capturing the path as an immutable string at call time so a variable reused across several directories doesn't leak a stale reference. (Companion ticket BL-458's live-orphan reaper is still in flight and is not yet part of this landed slice.)

**A periodic sweep now clears the existing stock of stale acceptance-test sandboxes from `/tmp` (BL-413).** BL-459 above bounds new accumulation going forward; this bounds what had already piled up. `sandbox_sweep_lib.bb`'s pure `removable?` predicate (allowlist-only known prefixes, staleness, no live process rooted in the entry, the swarm's own legacy socket dir excluded first and unconditionally) is wired into `operator_runtime.bb`'s existing tick loop as a bounded-per-tick `sandbox-sweep!`, reading its temp root and the legacy socket dir through the same redirectable env-seam convention `kill_all_swarm.sh` already established — it never touches the real `/tmp` in a test. **Cleaner pass, same ticket:** the `/proc` cwd+fd liveness scan this predicate depends on was deduped into a shared `proc_fd_scan_lib.bb` rather than living inline. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** the architect's own bounce is verified — liveness detection now checks a candidate directory's open file descriptors, not just its working directory, since a process can hold a sandbox dir open (a file handle) without that dir being its cwd, which the cwd-only check missed. No human-facing command or setting; this is internal test-infrastructure hygiene.

**The BL-413/BL-458 `/tmp` sweeps were a production no-op — they bounded the SCAN, not the DELETES — and now make provable per-tick progress (BL-460).** Live incident, Operator directive relayed 2026-07-16, against work QA had approved and closed the same day: both `sandbox-sweep!` (`operator_runtime.bb`) and `sweep!` (`fixture_reaper_sweep_lib.bb`) did `(take cap (list-entries root))` every tick — a bounded scan that always started at the same fixed readdir position, so a listing whose first `cap` (default 100) entries never contained a reapable one (live: 0 of the first 100, 76 orphan fixture processes untouched after 40+ ticks, `/tmp` growing) re-scanned that same dead window forever. The pure `removable?`/`reapable?` predicates from BL-413/BL-458 were correct and untouched; the defect was entirely in the windowing. Fix: a new shared `bounded_delete_sweep_lib.bb` maintains a persisted cursor that advances every tick over a stable sorted listing and wraps at the end, so both sweeps cover the whole directory over `ceil(count/cap)` ticks regardless of how many leading entries are non-reapable; `record-tick!` (added in a same-ticket cleaner pass) dedupes the cursor-persist and reaped/nothing-streak bookkeeping both callers had hand-rolled around it. Both sweeps now log a reap-summary line when they remove something and a periodic (not per-tick) nothing-found line otherwise — previously the reaper logged nothing at all and the dir sweep logged only on a removal, so a silent no-op was indistinguishable from success. `sandbox_sweep_lib.bb`'s allowlist gained 9 prefixes observed at volume in production, all traced to plain Vitest `mkTmpDir` fixtures in `extension/test/*.test.js` (no process spawning, so they belong to the dir sweep, not the reaper's process-killing allowlist) — allowlist-only, never a glob. No new human-facing command or setting; this is the same internal test-infrastructure-hygiene category as BL-412/BL-413/BL-458/BL-459, and the acceptance contract requires the fix to be proven on the live production box (orphan process count and `/tmp` entry count actually falling over successive ticks), not only in a fixture.

**A new `mono-rotate` pack lets ONE resident agent process serve the whole pipeline in turn, for hosts too memory-constrained to run one process per role (BL-448).** An Operator directive: FES's second-swarm host (15GB) OOM-crashed under a full swarm, so mono-rotate becomes FES's new default bring-up, superseding BL-439's 2-pack (BL-439 reshaped in the same pass to depend on and point at it). The human fixed the design up front: **all quality gates stay full-strength** — acceptance, coverage, mutation/no-surviving-mutants, CRAP<=6, QA's final pass — the memory saving comes only from one resident process, never from a lighter gate; slower wall-clock is the accepted cost. `swarmforge/packs/mono-rotate.conf` declares `config rotation sequential` plus the full coder → cleaner → architect → hardener → documenter → QA window list (the coordinator stays separately auto-provisioned, per BL-243, never part of the rotation); `is_sequential_dormant` (`swarmforge.sh`) is the new gating logic that still provisions every role's own worktree and `roles.tsv` entry (so mailbox resolution is correct the instant the resident agent becomes that role) but launches a real tmux session/process only for the first window line. `swarmforge/packs/mono-rotate.prompt` is the resident agent's own overlay: each pipeline role's `swarmforge/roles/<role>.prompt` stays the unmodified authority for that role's substance, and the overlay adds only the rotation step — once a role's handoff is sent, the agent looks up the next role's worktree path in `roles.tsv`, exports `SWARMFORGE_ROLE`, `cd`s in, re-reads the constitution and that role's prompt as if freshly started, then runs `ready_for_next.sh` to pick up the very handoff it just sent. The ticket's own central risk — SwarmForge's quality model rests on role INDEPENDENCE, and one agent playing both sides of a bounce is a self-review — is named explicitly rather than papered over: the overlay instructs the agent to evaluate each role's work as a genuinely fresh, skeptical reader, not from what it remembers deciding a minute ago, and documents that an automated context-reset-and-rebootstrap watcher (closing that gap for real) is a deferred, architect-owned mechanism decision, not part of this pass. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** added a boundary assertion (`test_rotation_sequential_pack.sh`) proving the LAST pipeline role (QA), immediately adjacent to the always-resident coordinator, is also correctly sequential-dormant — the existing middle-role assertions alone couldn't catch an off-by-one at the upper bound. New human-facing surface: `./swarm <target> --pack mono-rotate` launches this pack.

**The coordinator's Operator topic now carries a full voice-note conversation, not just text (BL-426 slice 1).** Human-requested audio channel: a voice note the human sends into the standing Operator topic (BL-346) is transcribed to text before it reaches the coordinator on the existing text-delivery path, and the coordinator's text reply is synthesized back to a spoken voice note (plus the text transcript alongside, for skimmability) sent to the same topic — multi-turn conversation falls out for free, since the Operator topic already carries context across turns. `decideVoiceUpdateAction` (`telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts`) is the pure inbound decision — a voice note in the coordinator's Operator topic from the authorised principal resolves to `transcribe` (carrying the voice file's `file_id`); a non-principal's voice note is `refuse`; a voice note in any other topic is `not-applicable`, so BL-425's per-role steering topics and every other existing route are untouched by this slice. `attemptVoiceDelivery` is the adapter-driven half: it downloads the voice note and calls the injected `transcribeVoice` adapter, then delivers the transcript on the same path an ordinary text message already uses, and marks the turn voice-originated (`markVoiceOriginatedTurn`) so the reply side knows to speak back. On the way out, `synthesizeVoiceReplyIfNeeded` checks that marker on the coordinator's reply and, if set, calls the injected `synthesizeVoice` adapter and `sendVoice`s the result to the same topic alongside the text reply already sent — a TTS failure degrades silently to text-only rather than losing the answer. A text message in the coordinator topic is completely unaffected (no transcription, no voice-out). Failure posture follows the BL-389 precedent: a transient STT failure does not advance the Telegram offset and is retried, never silently dropped; a structurally un-processable voice note (empty/wrong format) is a deliberate drop and the offset advances so it can never park redelivery forever. STT and TTS are provider-adapter seams (`transcribeVoiceNote`/`synthesizeVoiceReply`, `telegram-front-desk-bot.ts`) wired to OpenAI (Whisper for STT, `tts-1`/`alloy` for TTS) behind a new **`OPENAI_API_KEY`** environment variable read in the extension host only (never written to the target repo or a commit, per the secrets rule) — absent, voice I/O is simply not wired and the bot behaves exactly as before this ticket. No new human-facing command; the human can now speak to the coordinator's Operator topic and get a spoken reply back, and text conversation there is unchanged. Scope is the coordinator's Operator topic only — voice for the other seven roles' topics is a tracked, parked follow-up (depends on BL-425) not built in this slice.

**Acceptance step files now reap the detached process trees they spawn, on abnormal exit too, plus a standalone reaper for whatever a crashed run already left behind (BL-458).** Live incident, Operator directive relayed 2026-07-16: four orphaned test mini-swarms (12 stray `claude` agents, 4 `front_desk_supervisor.bb` trees with live bridge+bot children) survived ~17.8h after a Jul-15 acceptance run, reparented to init, ~1.45 GB RAM, their bots 404-hammering `api.telegram.org`. The root cause is structural, not a one-off: `launch_front_desk.sh` ends with `nohup bb <supervisor> ... &`, and `role_lifecycle.sh`'s `create_role_session` starts a detached `tmux -S <socket>` server — both deliberately detach and reparent to init, so teardown can never rely on child-process death and must hunt-and-kill by pidfile/root-path/socket instead. `specs/pipeline/steps/lib/fixtureReaper.js` is the shared prevention half: `onAbnormalExit(fn)` installs one `'exit'`/`'SIGINT'`/`'SIGTERM'` handler set per process and lets each step file register its own kill callback against it (rather than each file's proven fixture-specific kill logic being replaced), so cleanup now fires even when a scenario throws before its own inline teardown or the runner itself is killed; `track(root)`/`reap(root)` build on the same primitive for the front-desk pidfile shape. All four named offenders (`frontDeskHeadlessLauncherSteps.js`, which previously had no safety net beyond inline teardown in terminal `Then` steps, plus `frontDeskSurvivesRebootSteps.js`, `mergedCodeReachesDaemonsSteps.js`, `roleLifecycleParkUnneededSteps.js`, which each had only a `process.on('exit', ...)` handler that never fires on SIGTERM/SIGINT/timeout/OOM) now go through it. The auto-clean half mirrors BL-412/BL-413's shape: `fixture_reaper_lib.bb`'s pure `reapable?` predicate (allowlist-only known fixture prefixes, staleness, with the live swarm's own socket root excluded first and unconditionally, regardless of age) plus `fixture_reaper_sweep_lib.bb`'s real wiring (kill any process rooted in a reaped root via `/proc/<pid>/cwd`, kill any tmux server under it, delete the tree) is wired into `operator_runtime.bb`'s existing tick loop alongside the BL-412/BL-413 sweeps, ordered so a process this reaper kills lets a later `sandbox-sweep!` tick remove the now-emptied root; `reap_stale_test_fixtures.bb` exposes the same real sweep as a standalone CLI for ad hoc/manual use, mirroring `resolve_swarm_socket.bb`'s Babashka-callable-without-FFI pattern. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** added direct unit coverage of `reap()`'s own file-parsing branches (missing/corrupt `status.json` falling through to the pidfile kill, missing pidfile, tmux-socket kill, idempotent double-reap) — the acceptance suite's SIGTERM scenario had only ever proven the signal-handling mechanism against one always-complete fixture, never these branches, and never touches `track()`/`onAbnormalExit()` themselves, which install real signal handlers on the current process. No new human-facing command or setting; this is internal test-infrastructure hygiene, same category as BL-412/BL-413/BL-459 — reconciling today's four live orphans falls out of this reaper rather than a manual kill, per the Operator directive.

**A standing "Recert" Telegram topic now carries the whole Gherkin recertification loop in-chat — validate, amend, delete — giving the previously-dark recert store its first live writer (BL-450).** Human-requested full move out of the PWA, distinct from BL-339's notify-and-deep-link-only shape (which the human explicitly declined): before this ticket, `recert-state.json` had zero production writers (`confirmScenario`/`writeRecertStore`/`appendRecertProposal` existed since BL-150 but were only ever called from tests), so `lastReviewedIso` never advanced and the oldest-first batch never rotated outside the PWA's `mailto:`-only flow. `conciergeTick.ts` now posts the current oldest-unreviewed scenario (`computeRecertBatch(targetPath, 1)`, the same derivation the PWA itself uses — never a second selection) into a standing Recert topic one scenario at a time, edit-in-place and edge-triggered off a durable `recertPosted` marker in `TickState` — a same-scenario tick touches nothing, and an empty queue posts nothing at all rather than a placeholder (unlike the Approvals roster/Pipeline Board syncs, which always render something). `recertPosting.ts` renders the scenario id, title, Gherkin text, and the three reply verbs; `recertPostingSync.ts` is the adapter-driven I/O half, reusing the same `editInPlaceMessageSync.ts` core the Approvals roster and Pipeline Board already share. Reply routing is a new reserved subject, `RECERT_SUBJECT_ID`, checked in `telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts`'s `decideUpdateAction` ahead of the ordinary post-existing-subject branch (the same posture as the Approvals topic's own `APPROVALS_SUBJECT_ID` check) and parsed by `recertTopicReply.ts`'s `classifyRecertTopicReply` — a scenario-id-bound grammar (`validate <id>`, `amend <id> <text>`, `delete <id>`), a separate module from the Approvals topic's bare-verb grammar since recert is a distinct domain (Gherkin scenarios, not backlog tickets) with its own two-step delete confirmation. **Verb mapping, matching the human's chosen gate:** `validate` calls `confirmScenario`/`writeRecertStore` directly (low-risk, a timestamp bump); `amend`/`delete` only ever `appendRecertProposal` a proposal into the existing `recert_proposals/<month>.jsonl` queue for specifier review — no chat reply ever edits a `.feature` file directly. `delete <id>` itself queues nothing: it checks the named scenario is genuinely up for recert, then arms a pending-delete marker and asks for an explicit "confirm" reply before `queueRecertDeleteProposal` runs (BL-150 recert-04) — a bare "confirm" with nothing pending is a silent drop, never treated as one more unrecognized reply. A reply naming a scenario not currently up for recert (a stale or fabricated id) is surfaced back into the topic, never silently applied (front-desk-operator-fabricates-backlog-state memory) or fabricated as accepted. **Cleaner pass, same ticket:** extracted `plainTextEditInPlaceAdapters()` so the roster and recert posting adapters stop duplicating the same postMessage/editMessage lambdas, and collapsed the Approvals/Recert reserved-subject dispatch in `decideUpdateAction`/`processMessageUpdate` into shared helpers to bring both functions' CRAP back under the article's <=6 gate after the new Recert branch pushed it to 7; added the missing `ensureRecertTopic` tests mirroring `ensureApprovalsTopic`'s existing coverage. New human-facing surface: a standing "Recert" Telegram topic with reply grammar `validate <id>` / `amend <id> <text>` / `delete <id>` then `confirm`. The PWA's recert view and BL-339's deep-link notify are unchanged by this ticket — retiring them is BL-451, sequenced after this loop is proven live.

**One standing "Approvals" Telegram topic now aggregates every ticket awaiting approval, with a live roster, replacing the old per-ticket ask (BL-434).** Human-requested, via Telegram, 2026-07-15: today's approval ask lives scattered across each ticket's own BL topic (BL-357/BL-408/BL-409/BL-410), so the human has to hunt across topics to find what is waiting. The human's considered shape, resolved via `AskUserQuestion` then corrected on a first self-unblocked narrower cut: **BOTH** — a live index AND acting in the one topic. `topicRouter.ts`'s `routeEvent` now dispatches `ApprovalRequested` to its own `routeApprovalRequestedEvent` path instead of the old per-ticket reuse/create — it posts the ask into the ONE standing Approvals topic (`ensureApprovalsTopic`, create-once/reuse exactly like the existing standing Operator topic), and the ask text now NAMES the ticket ("`BL-123 needs your approval... Reply here with "approve BL-123"...`") since one topic now carries every ticket's ask at once. **The one genuinely new mechanism** is `pendingApprovalReply.ts`'s `classifyApprovalsTopicReply` — a separate, narrower parser from the existing per-ticket-topic `classifyApprovalReplyAction` (the two topics have different reply grammars: bare "approve" vs "approve `<id>`"), which `telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts`'s `decideUpdateAction` now consults first for any reply landing in the reserved `APPROVALS_SUBJECT_ID` subject, ahead of the ordinary post-existing-subject branch. It reuses the EXISTING `recordApprovalReply`/`recordRejectionReply` adapters — never a second recording path — and their own boolean `changed` result to tell "this id really was pending, now recorded" from "this id was not pending", surfacing the latter back into the Approvals topic (`notifyApprovalsTopic`) rather than silently dropping it (front-desk-operator-fabricates-backlog-state memory); both an unrecognized reply and a not-pending id are DELIBERATE DROPS, so the poll offset always advances past either rather than parking (the BL-389 drop-vs-failure distinction). **The live index half:** `approvalsRoster.ts`'s pure `renderApprovalsRoster` renders the current `pendingApprovalFor` set (sorted by id, so the rendered text is deterministic tick over tick) into one roster message, which `approvalsRosterSync.ts` posts-or-edits IN PLACE, change-gated on the rendered text itself (never a set diff) — a genuine pending-set change edits the one message; an unchanged tick touches nothing, so this never becomes the first-tick unthrottled mass-edit storm the engineering article warns about (it is always exactly one message). **Cleaner pass, same ticket:** the create-once/post-or-edit control flow was byte-for-byte duplicated between the new roster sync and the existing Pipeline Board sync, so both now share one `editInPlaceMessageSync.ts` core, each supplying only its own render function and adapter. Per BL-424, a ticket's own topic-icon awaiting-approval state keeps working even though the ask itself no longer posts there: `ensurePerTicketTopicForIcon` still creates the per-ticket topic (never posts into it) purely so the icon sync has somewhere to set the icon. No change to how approval is recorded on disk (`human_approval` YAML field, BL-409 reject-reason sanitization) — only where the ask is posted and how a reply is routed to a ticket. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** killed a surviving Gherkin mutant and brought CRAP back under the article's threshold. New human-facing surface: a standing "Approvals" Telegram topic, and the reply grammar in that topic is now `approve <id>` / `reject <id> <reason>` rather than bare `approve`/`reject <reason>`.

**An agent's clarifying question now surfaces directly on Telegram — as a native poll when it has discrete options, starting with the specifier (BL-466).** Human-requested via the Operator front desk, 2026-07-16, for iso-functionality with the in-editor `AskUserQuestion` UI: previously a specifier's question reached the human only indirectly through the Concierge's derived-event machinery. `operator_ask.bb <project-root> --thread <SUP-###> --question <q> [--options '["a","b"]']` now accepts an optional `--options` (a JSON array of 2+ strings); `parse-options` (`operator_lib.bb`) normalizes it to `nil` on any malformed input (invalid JSON, a bare number, an array of non-strings) rather than crashing and losing the question outright, so a bad `--options` value degrades to the same plain-message path as no options at all, never a dropped ask. Every reply-outbox entry `operator_ask.bb` writes — including its escalate-once and re-home continuations (BL-306/BL-354) — is now marked `agentQuestion: true`, alongside `options` when present, so the front-desk bot can distinguish an agent's own question from an ordinary Operator/approval message without a second channel. A new standing "Agent Questions" Telegram topic (`AGENT_QUESTIONS_SUBJECT_ID`, create-once/reuse exactly like the existing standing Operator/Approvals topics) is where these land: `telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts`'s `deliverAgentQuestion` renders a native poll via `telegramClient.ts`'s new `sendPoll` wrapper when `options` has 2+ entries, or a plain message otherwise — the two-or-none contract the ticket specifies, never a one-option poll. The Agent Questions side channel is attempted LAST, after the ordinary per-ticket/Operator/Approvals routing, so it only ever fires for a genuine `agentQuestion` record. The human's answer flows back through BL-325's EXISTING awaiting-answer/unblock machinery, never a parallel path: a poll vote or an in-topic reply resolves to the pending question's own `SUP-###` thread via `resolvePollThread`/`getPendingAgentQuestionThread`, backed by a `readPollMap`/`writePollMap` poll-id-to-thread lookup and the runtime's own `awaiting-answer.json` read — both newly exported and given fixture-backed wiring tests (including a break-then-fix proof that the `awaiting-answer.json` read is load-bearing, since the wiring test's fixture had never actually placed the file). An unanswered question inherits BL-306/BL-325's bounded-await posture unchanged — escalate once, then drop the awaiting state — so a poll can never block an agent forever. **Hardener pass, same ticket:** the cooldown gate (BL-149/BL-463) skip-cooldown'd the touched TS files and Babashka scripts this pass, each independently touched by a sibling ticket on `main` within the preceding few hours; Gherkin mutation was out of scope (the feature file uses plain `Scenario`, no `Scenario Outline`/`Examples`). No change to the pipeline's derived-event/topic-routing machinery for tickets or approvals — this is a new, narrower delivery path scoped to an agent's own clarifying question. New human-facing surface: a standing "Agent Questions" Telegram topic; a discrete-option question now appears there as a native poll, an open-ended one as a plain message, and either resolves back to the asking agent exactly like any other BL-325 answer.

**A single `build_freshness_cli.bb sync` pass now settles operator_runtime's staleness instead of requiring a second pass (BL-433).** Root cause, confirmed in code: `restart-operator-group!` relaunches the stale `operator_runtime.bb` process asynchronously and returns immediately, without clearing or waiting on its `status.json`; `run-sync!` then reports from a snapshot gathered BEFORE the restart. So even a perfect restart's own sync output — and any immediate `report` right after it — still showed operator_runtime stale, and the coordinator had been papering over this by re-syncing on every bookkeeping cycle. Fix, mirroring the front-desk group's own restart path (which already deletes its `status.json` and relaunches synchronously, so it never exhibited this race): `restart-operator-group!` now deletes operator_runtime's `status.json` before relaunching, then blocks up to a human-approved 10s for it to reappear with `:build_sha` == `main` HEAD; `run-sync!`'s report reflects that settled post-restart state, not the pre-restart snapshot. If the new process never publishes fresh status within the 10s bound, `sync` fails loudly (non-zero exit) rather than hanging or falsely reporting fresh. Front-desk and handoffd sync behavior is unchanged — only the operator-group race is closed. No new human-facing command; this is an internal fix to the swarm's own build-freshness tool (`swarmforge/scripts/build_freshness_cli.bb`), removing the need for the coordinator's re-sync workaround.

**A live production caller now actually reaches the poll path above (BL-466 wiring fix).** QA bounced the ticket above as shipped-but-dark: `--options` and its whole poll machinery were fully built, unit- and acceptance-tested, but the only real (non-test) invocation site of `operator_ask.bb` — the disposable Operator LLM's own ASK instructions in `swarmforge/roles/operator.prompt` — still only ever constructed the plain `--question` form, so a specifier's discrete-option question would degrade to a plain message forever in the live swarm (the same "correct and green but invoked by nothing" class already on file for `mutation_cooldown_gate.bb`, BL-149). Fix: `operator.prompt`'s ASK section now instructs the Operator to also pass `--options '["<choice-1>","<choice-2>",...]'` when the question it is relaying has a small, fixed set of discrete answers (e.g. a specifier's `AskUserQuestion`-style decision menu), and to omit it for a genuinely open-ended question — degrading, exactly as `parse-options` already handles, to the plain-message form. No code changes; this closes the wiring gap in the Operator's own prompt instructions, the one real caller BL-466's poll machinery needed.

**The front-desk standing topic is rebranded Operator -> Concierge: bell icon (🛎), "Concierge" label (BL-453).** Human-requested rebrand, glyph human-chosen 2026-07-16 ("The bell is fine" = 🛎), superseding BL-418's opera-house (🏛) choice for this one standing topic — the support/intake (🎟), approvals (📋), and recert (📜) standing-topic icons are unchanged. `STANDING_TOPIC_ICON.operator` in `topicIcon.ts` changes from 🏛 to 🛎; the live tick's `syncStandingTopicIcons` never re-touches an already-seen topic on its own, so an existing install's front-desk topic only picks up the new sticker via a one-time `backfill-standing-topic-icons.js` run — the same operational step BL-342/BL-418 already established, not new wiring. `OPERATOR_TOPIC_NAME` in `telegramFrontDeskBotCore.ts` changes from `'Operator'` to `'Concierge'`; since the front-desk topic is already created and bound for any existing install, a name-constant change alone would never reach it, so `telegram-front-desk-bot.ts`'s `ensureOperatorTopic` gained `syncStandingTopicTitleIfNeeded` — on the existing "reuse" path it renames the live topic via `editForumTopic` exactly once (a durable, bot-owned, machine-local `telegram-standing-topic-titles.json` record, gitignored under `.swarmforge/`, prevents re-editing an already-correct title on every restart), while a brand-new install's create path gets the new name for free and records it immediately so the reuse-path check never fires a redundant rename. `OPERATOR_SUBJECT_ID` (the durable binding/ownership key) is unchanged — only the icon and the display name move; the existing bound topic is reused, never re-minted. Out of scope: the broader Operator -> Concierge rename of message signatures/bylines is a separate, still-unfiled follow-up. No new human-facing command; the same front-desk topic now shows the bell icon and is titled "Concierge" instead of the opera house and "Operator".

**Pipeline board: the new message now posts before the old one is deleted, so a board is always visible (BL-468).** Human-requested directly 2026-07-16: "first add the new one, then remove the old one, so there is at least always 1 to look at." Before this, BL-462's repost-at-bottom mechanism deleted the old board message FIRST, then posted the fresh one — a window with zero board messages in the topic, and if the fresh post then failed, the old message was already gone while `state.messageId` still pointed at it. `pipelineBoardSync.ts`'s `postBoardMessage` now reorders to post-new-then-delete-old: on a successful post, the prior message is deleted best-effort only AFTER the new one exists (the delete's existing best-effort posture — a failed or already-gone delete never blocks); on a FAILED post, the prior message is left alone and the outcome reports a failed post with the prior `messageId` still tracked in state, so the existing board stays visible. No renderer, change-gate, or adapter-interface change — only the call order inside `postBoardMessage` and the failed-post branch. Two board messages can briefly coexist during the swap; this is compatible with BL-467's pin sync (pins the newest, continuously unpins the old) and BL-465's render. No new human-facing command; the "Pipeline Board" Telegram topic now never has a moment with no board message visible, even across a post failure.

**Pipeline-board stage map: a differently-cased ticket id in a handoff header no longer risks silently dropping an active ticket from the board (BL-471).** Defensive hardening of BL-464's authoritative ticket->stage source, from a coordinator note whose specific live claim did not reproduce (verified 2026-07-16: every real handoff header in the tree already uses upper-case `BL-`, and the reported "missing" ticket was simply not held by any role at the time — correct behaviour, not a bug). The latent gap itself is real: `swarmforge/scripts/pipeline_stage_lib.bb` joined a role's held-ticket id (extracted verbatim, whatever case a note/task header used) against the canonical, always-upper-case `id:` field of each active backlog item by an exact-case `contains?` — so a handoff header that ever led with a lower- or mixed-case id (e.g. a note whose `message:` begins "bl-447 ...") would fail that membership test and vanish from the board with no error. The ticket-id join is now case-insensitive: the extracted header id is canonicalized to upper-case before both the active-set membership check and the stage-map reconciliation, so a handoff header leading with a differently-cased id resolves to the same active ticket and appears on the board at its correct stage. Kept pure/side-effect-free, matching the file's existing posture. No new human-facing command; this is a robustness fix to the internal "Pipeline Board" Telegram topic's ticket-stage data source, not a behavior change for any header that was already upper-case (i.e. every real header observed in production).

**Swarm stop (drain or emergency), restart, and a timed intake-freeze pause are now driven from a guarded Telegram control topic (BL-423).** Human-requested via the Operator front desk (2026-07-15, amended same day for drain/emergency-stop split and timed pause): drive swarm stop/start from the phone without needing the VS Code extension host in the foreground. Three verbs, one dedicated control topic, sent by the authorised principal only — the same principal/topic guard BL-408/409 already use for Telegram verbs, applied here to a destructive/administrative surface for the first time:
- **`/stop`** posts one confirmation with two action buttons plus Cancel — **Drain & stop** and **Emergency stop** — executing nothing until a button is tapped; there is no separate `/forcestop` verb. Emergency stop tears down immediately with no drain wait. Drain stop waits for every role's `inbox/in_process` to empty first, bounded by a drain timeout (default 10 minutes, human-set, env-overridable for tests); if the pipeline has not drained by then, teardown is forced and the outcome is reported `forced` rather than `drained`. Both modes reap every swarm-owned process — tmux windows and any reparented orphaned vitest workers, the exact class behind the BL-422 OOM-spiral — through `kill_all_swarm.sh`'s socket-scoped path.
- **`/restart`** posts a confirmation and, on confirm, reuses the existing sanctioned bounce path (`remote_bounce.sh` sentinel -> the extension host's `bounceWatcher`/`bounceDrain`/`bounceAck`) rather than a new respawn mechanism, streaming each bounce phase (draining -> stopping -> relaunching -> done/failed) back into the control topic. A relaunch that creates tmux windows but never actually bootstraps agents into them (the earlier `SWARM_CONTROL_LOST` half-launch failure mode) is reported `failed`, not `done` — the verify-ready step checks agents actually bootstrapped, not merely that windows exist.
- **`/pause`** posts a duration menu (15 min / 1 hr / 4 hr / Until I resume); picking a duration IS the action, no separate confirm, since pause is non-destructive and auto-reverting. The semantic is FREEZE NEW-WORK INTAKE only — agents stay alive, in-flight parcels finish, no new paused item is promoted — never a process suspend or a teardown+relaunch. The freeze rides the coordinator's own effective-active-backlog-depth read (`swarmforge/scripts/backlog_depth_lib.bb`, the same primitive the health-throttling circuit breaker already uses to drop the cap to 0): a live, unexpired pause marker under `.swarmforge/` (gitignored, host-persisted, reached through a redirectable env seam) makes that computation return 0, so the existing promotion gate freezes with no new per-caller logic. A timed pick auto-resumes and posts a "resumed" notice to the control topic when its duration elapses (evaluated against an injected clock via the daemon's existing sweep cadence); "Until I resume" has no timer and stays frozen until an explicit `Resume now` tap, which restores intake immediately and clears any pending auto-resume.

Every inline-button tap (a stop-mode pick, a pause-duration pick, Resume) RE-APPLIES the principal + topic guards — an unauthorised tap on someone else's pending control button is refused with no swarm action, since anyone in a Telegram group can tap another human's button. An unauthorised sender's verb, or any of the three verbs sent outside the dedicated control topic, is likewise refused/ignored with no action. The verb/callback parse, guards, confirm state machine, and pause state machine are one pure host-side module (`telegramControlCore.ts`, mirroring `operatorDecideStatus.ts`'s shape): given a message/callback, principal, topic, pending-confirm state, pause state, and the current time, it decides `ignore | prompt-stop-modes | prompt-restart-confirm | execute-emergency-stop | execute-drain-stop | execute-restart | cancel | post-pause-menu | apply-pause | auto-resume | resume-now | refuse` — unit-tested with fixtures, no live Telegram or tmux. New human-facing surface: a dedicated Telegram control topic with `/stop`, `/restart`, and `/pause` (plus their confirmation buttons and, while paused, a `Resume now` button).

**Pipeline board render round 2: a short kebab slug leads every entry, PK/AA per-line labels are dropped in favour of their own sections, and a tappable GitHub link list rides below the grid (BL-465).** Human-requested via the Operator front desk 2026-07-16, refined the same day ("add the slug back to the pipeline board grid — there will be room enough for 2 or 3 words"): the aligned stage GRID's dedicated slug column now shows only a short (2-3 word) kebab slug derived from the ticket's backlog filename (e.g. `BL-467-pipeline-board-only-pin` -> `pipeline-board-only-pin`) — the grid has no separate title column to widen, so it carries the slug alone. The BELOW-GRID lists (parked / awaiting-approval / paused / root-intake / recently-closed) lead each entry with that same kebab slug and then fill the remaining landscape width with more of the truncated title than before. This deliberately supersedes BL-462's own "wider slug in the grid" contract (`deriveTicketSlug`/`PIPELINE_BOARD_SLUG_MAX_LENGTH` used to size the grid's own slug column for a wide truncated title); a follow-up retires BL-462's now-stale grid-slug scenario the same way BL-470 retired BL-452's superseded scenarios. The redundant per-line "PK" label is dropped from the parked list (the section header already says parked); awaiting-approval keeps its distinction via its own "AWAITING APPROVAL:" section instead of a per-line "AA" label. Two new sections appear alongside parked: PAUSED (`backlog/paused/` items) and ROOT-INTAKE (raw `backlog/` root asks), plus a RECENTLY-CLOSED section.
